Pass --comment to post findings as inline PR comments, or --fix to apply the findings to the working tree after the review.\n- simplify: Review the changed code for reuse, simplification, efficiency, and altitude cleanups, then apply the fixes. {"parentUuid":"21f2b3a6-e780-4505-9dd3-90bdc07a34e9","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"ff6c8414-3cf8-4eac-9dd8-a003a75cddc1","agentId":"a1fb0fb2cb5fa37d4","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01MrkSvHQsrhZWFwTwvE2RXk","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t//! Statistical price-intelligence primitives for the integrity engine.\n2\t//!\n3\t//! All functions operate on **sorted** or **unsorted** slices of `i64` amounts\n4\t//! (won). They are pure — no I/O, no async — so they live in the kernel crate\n5\t//! and can be called from any layer.\n6\t//!\n7\t//! ## Small-sample guard\n8\t//!\n9\t//! Statistical outlier flags are only reliable once a baseline of at least\n10\t//! [`MIN_SAMPLE_SIZE`] peers exists. Below that threshold every function that\n11\t//! would produce a false-precision score returns [`PriceIntelResult::Sparse`]\n12\t//! instead of a numeric value. Callers that display this to users should show\n13\t//! \"근거 부족 (데이터 부족)\" rather than any numeric flag.\n14\t//!\n15\t//! ## Confidence tiers\n16\t//!\n17\t//! | Sample size | Tier |\n18\t//! |---|---|\n19\t//! | < 5 | `Sparse` (no flag) |\n20\t//! | 5–14 | `Low` |\n21\t//! | 15–29 | `Medium` |\n22\t//! | ≥ 30 | `High` |\n23\t//!\n24\t//! These thresholds are deliberately conservative. A false positive on a\n25\t//! legitimate 기안 is more damaging to trust than missing a suspicious one.\n26\t\n27\t/// Minimum peer count required before any statistical outlier flag is issued.\n28\tpub const MIN_SAMPLE_SIZE: usize = 5;\n29\t\n30\t/// Confidence tier for a statistical finding.\n31\t#[derive(\n32\t    Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize,\n33\t)]\n34\t#[serde(rename_all = \"snake_case\")]\n35\tpub enum Confidence {\n36\t    Low,\n37\t    Medium,\n38\t    High,\n39\t}\n40\t\n41\timpl Confidence {\n42\t    #[must_use]\n43\t    pub const fn from_sample_size(n: usize) -> Self {\n44\t        if n >= 30 {\n45\t            Self::High\n46\t        } else if n >= 15 {\n47\t            Self::Medium\n48\t        } else {\n49\t            Self::Low\n50\t        }\n51\t    }\n52\t}\n53\t\n54\t/// Result of a statistical outlier check.\n55\t///\n56\t/// [`Sparse`] means the sample is too small to produce a reliable signal.\n57\t/// Callers should surface this as \"근거 부족 (데이터 부족)\", never as a flag.\n58\t#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize)]\n59\t#[serde(rename_all = \"snake_case\", tag = \"kind\")]\n60\tpub enum PriceIntelResult {\n61\t    /// Too few peers to compute a reliable statistic. Never produce a finding\n62\t    /// from this — a false flag on scarce data harms legitimate users.\n63\t    Sparse {\n64\t        /// How many peers were available (for diagnostic display).\n65\t        peer_count: usize,\n66\t    },\n67\t    /// The sample is large enough; here is the computed signal.\n68\t    Computed {\n69\t        /// Z-score of the target value against the peer distribution.\n70\t        /// Positive = above the mean; negative = below.\n71\t        z_score: f64,\n72\t        /// Median absolute deviation (MAD) ratio: `|target - median| / MAD`.\n73\t        /// More robust than z-score for small-to-medium skewed distributions.\n74\t        /// `None` if MAD == 0 (all peers are identical).\n75\t        mad_ratio: Option<f64>,\n76\t        /// IQR fence check. `true` if `target > Q3 + 1.5 * IQR`.\n77\t        above_iqr_fence: bool,\n78\t        /// Percentile of the target value within the peer distribution (0–100).\n79\t        percentile: f64,\n80\t        /// Peer sample size (for confidence display).\n81\t        peer_count: usize,\n82\t        /// Statistical confidence tier.\n83\t        confidence: Confidence,\n84\t    },\n85\t}\n86\t\n87\timpl PriceIntelResult {\n88\t    /// Returns `true` if the result is sparse (too few peers).\n89\t    #[must_use]\n90\t    pub const fn is_sparse(&self) -> bool {\n91\t        matches!(self, Self::Sparse { .. })\n92\t    }\n93\t\n94\t    /// Heuristic \"is this suspicious?\" check combining all signals.\n95\t    ///\n96\t    /// Returns `None` for sparse results (never flag).\n97\t    /// For computed results, returns a score in [0.0, 1.0] where higher means\n98\t    /// more suspicious. The caller maps this to a [`Severity`] threshold.\n99\t    #[must_use]\n100\t    pub fn suspicion_score(&self) -> Option<f64> {\n101\t        match self {\n102\t            Self::Sparse { .. } => None,\n103\t            Self::Computed {\n104\t                z_score,\n105\t                mad_ratio,\n106\t                above_iqr_fence,\n107\t                percentile,\n108\t                ..\n109\t            } => {\n110\t                // Weight the signals: z-score (normalized), MAD ratio, IQR fence,\n111\t                // and raw percentile. All clamped to [0,1] before weighting.\n112\t                let z_norm = (z_score.abs() / 4.0).min(1.0); // 4σ → max signal\n113\t                let mad_norm = mad_ratio.map(|m| (m / 5.0).min(1.0)).unwrap_or(0.0); // 5× MAD → max signal\n114\t                let iqr_signal = if *above_iqr_fence { 1.0 } else { 0.0 };\n115\t                let pct_norm = ((*percentile - 90.0).max(0.0) / 10.0).min(1.0); // top 10% → max signal\n116\t\n117\t                // Only flag HIGH percentile (above average is normal; we want\n118\t                // extreme outliers on the HIGH side — overpayment risk).\n119\t                if *z_score < 0.0 {\n120\t                    // Below mean — not a price-inflation concern.\n121\t                    return Some(0.0);\n122\t                }\n123\t\n124\t                let score = 0.35 * z_norm + 0.30 * mad_norm + 0.20 * iqr_signal + 0.15 * pct_norm;\n125\t                Some(score.clamp(0.0, 1.0))\n126\t            }\n127\t        }\n128\t    }\n129\t}\n130\t\n131\t/// Compute price-intelligence statistics for a target amount against a peer\n132\t/// distribution.\n133\t///\n134\t/// # Arguments\n135\t/// * `target` — the amount under scrutiny (i64 won).\n136\t/// * `peers` — all amounts in the peer group INCLUDING `target` itself\n137\t///   (the detector fetches the whole distribution, which naturally contains\n138\t///   the row being checked). The function handles deduplication internally.\n139\t///\n140\t/// # Returns\n141\t/// [`PriceIntelResult::Sparse`] if `peers.len() < MIN_SAMPLE_SIZE`, otherwise\n142\t/// [`PriceIntelResult::Computed`] with full statistics.\n143\t///\n144\t/// # Panics\n145\t/// Never. All arithmetic uses checked or finite-safe operations.\n146\t#[must_use]\n147\tpub fn compute_price_intel(target: i64, peers: &[i64]) -> PriceIntelResult {\n148\t    let n = peers.len();\n149\t    if n < MIN_SAMPLE_SIZE {\n150\t        return PriceIntelResult::Sparse { peer_count: n };\n151\t    }\n152\t\n153\t    // Sort a copy for percentile / median / IQR.\n154\t    let mut sorted = peers.to_vec();\n155\t    sorted.sort_unstable();\n156\t\n157\t    let target_f = target as f64;\n158\t    let n_f = n as f64;\n159\t\n160\t    // Mean and standard deviation.\n161\t    let mean = sorted.iter().map(|&x| x as f64).sum::<f64>() / n_f;\n162\t    let variance = sorted\n163\t        .iter()\n164\t        .map(|&x| {\n165\t            let d = x as f64 - mean;\n166\t            d * d\n167\t        })\n168\t        .sum::<f64>()\n169\t        / n_f; // population variance (we have the full peer set, not a sample)\n170\t    let std_dev = variance.sqrt();\n171\t\n172\t    let z_score = if std_dev > 0.0 {\n173\t        (target_f - mean) / std_dev\n174\t    } else {\n175\t        0.0\n176\t    };\n177\t\n178\t    // Median and MAD (median absolute deviation).\n179\t    let median = percentile_sorted(&sorted, 50.0);\n180\t    let deviations: Vec<f64> = sorted.iter().map(|&x| (x as f64 - median).abs()).collect();\n181\t    let mad = {\n182\t        let mut dev_sorted = deviations.clone();\n183\t        dev_sorted.sort_by(f64::total_cmp);\n184\t        percentile_f64_sorted(&dev_sorted, 50.0)\n185\t    };\n186\t    let mad_ratio = if mad > 0.0 {\n187\t        Some((target_f - median).abs() / mad)\n188\t    } else {\n189\t        None\n190\t    };\n191\t\n192\t    // IQR fence.\n193\t    let q1 = percentile_sorted(&sorted, 25.0);\n194\t    let q3 = percentile_sorted(&sorted, 75.0);\n195\t    let iqr = q3 - q1;\n196\t    let upper_fence = q3 + 1.5 * iqr;\n197\t    let above_iqr_fence = target_f > upper_fence;\n198\t\n199\t    // Percentile of target.\n200\t    let rank = sorted.partition_point(|&x| (x as f64) < target_f);\n201\t    let percentile = if n == 1 {\n202\t        50.0\n203\t    } else {\n204\t        (rank as f64) / ((n - 1) as f64) * 100.0\n205\t    };\n206\t\n207\t    PriceIntelResult::Computed {\n208\t        z_score,\n209\t        mad_ratio,\n210\t        above_iqr_fence,\n211\t        percentile: percentile.clamp(0.0, 100.0),\n212\t        peer_count: n,\n213\t        confidence: Confidence::from_sample_size(n),\n214\t    }\n215\t}\n216\t\n217\t/// Compute the p-th percentile of a sorted `i64` slice using linear\n218\t/// interpolation (nearest-rank with linear interpolation for non-integer\n219\t/// positions).\n220\t///\n221\t/// `p` must be in `[0.0, 100.0]`. The slice must be non-empty and sorted.\n222\t#[must_use]\n223\tfn percentile_sorted(sorted: &[i64], p: f64) -> f64 {\n224\t    debug_assert!(!sorted.is_empty());\n225\t    debug_assert!((0.0..=100.0).contains(&p));\n226\t\n227\t    let n = sorted.len();\n228\t    if n == 1 {\n229\t        return sorted[0] as f64;\n230\t    }\n231\t\n232\t    let index = p / 100.0 * (n as f64 - 1.0);\n233\t    let lo = index.floor() as usize;\n234\t    let hi = (lo + 1).min(n - 1);\n235\t    let frac = index - lo as f64;\n236\t\n237\t    sorted[lo] as f64 * (1.0 - frac) + sorted[hi] as f64 * frac\n238\t}\n239\t\n240\t/// Same as [`percentile_sorted`] but for `f64` slices (used for MAD\n241\t/// computation).\n242\t#[must_use]\n243\tfn percentile_f64_sorted(sorted: &[f64], p: f64) -> f64 {\n244\t    debug_assert!(!sorted.is_empty());\n245\t\n246\t    let n = sorted.len();\n247\t    if n == 1 {\n248\t        return sorted[0];\n249\t    }\n250\t\n251\t    let index = p / 100.0 * (n as f64 - 1.0);\n252\t    let lo = index.floor() as usize;\n253\t    let hi = (lo + 1).min(n - 1);\n254\t    let frac = index - lo as f64;\n255\t\n256\t    sorted[lo] * (1.0 - frac) + sorted[hi] * frac\n257\t}\n258\t\n259\t#[cfg(test)]\n260\tmod tests {\n261\t    use super::*;\n262\t\n263\t    #[test]\n264\t    fn sparse_below_min_sample() {\n265\t        let result = compute_price_intel(100_000, &[100_000, 90_000, 80_000, 110_000]);\n266\t        assert!(matches!(result, PriceIntelResult::Sparse { peer_count: 4 }));\n267\t        assert!(result.is_sparse());\n268\t        assert!(result.suspicion_score().is_none());\n269\t    }\n270\t\n271\t    #[test]\n272\t    fn no_flag_for_below_mean() {\n273\t        let peers: Vec<i64> = vec![100_000, 110_000, 105_000, 98_000, 102_000, 107_000, 99_000];\n274\t        let result = compute_price_intel(80_000, &peers);\n275\t        let score = result.suspicion_score().unwrap();\n276\t        assert_eq!(score, 0.0, \"below-mean value should have zero suspicion\");\n277\t    }\n278\t\n279\t    #[test]\n280\t    fn high_suspicion_for_extreme_outlier() {\n281\t        // 10 normal peers, one extreme outlier target (10x the median).\n282\t        let peers: Vec<i64> = vec![\n283\t            100_000, 105_000, 98_000, 102_000, 110_000, 95_000, 108_000, 103_000, 99_000, 101_000,\n284\t        ];\n285\t        // Target is 10× the median.\n286\t        let result = compute_price_intel(1_000_000, &peers);\n287\t        match &result {\n288\t            PriceIntelResult::Computed {\n289\t                above_iqr_fence,\n290\t                z_score,\n291\t                ..\n292\t            } => {\n293\t                assert!(*above_iqr_fence, \"extreme value must be above IQR fence\");\n294\t                assert!(*z_score > 2.0, \"z-score must be high for extreme outlier\");\n295\t            }\n296\t            PriceIntelResult::Sparse { .. } => panic!(\"should not be sparse\"),\n297\t        }\n298\t        let score = result.suspicion_score().unwrap();\n299\t        assert!(\n300\t            score > 0.5,\n301\t            \"extreme outlier suspicion score should be high, got {score}\"\n302\t        );\n303\t    }\n304\t\n305\t    #[test]\n306\t    fn percentile_median_for_middle_value() {\n307\t        let peers: Vec<i64> = (1..=11).map(|i| i * 10_000).collect();\n308\t        let result = compute_price_intel(60_000, &peers);\n309\t        if let PriceIntelResult::Computed { percentile, .. } = result {\n310\t            // 60_000 is the exact median of 1..11 * 10_000.\n311\t            assert!(\n312\t                (percentile - 50.0).abs() < 1.0,\n313\t                \"median value should be near 50th percentile, got {percentile}\"\n314\t            );\n315\t        } else {\n316\t            panic!(\"expected Computed\");\n317\t        }\n318\t    }\n319\t\n320\t    #[test]\n321\t    fn confidence_tiers() {\n322\t        assert_eq!(Confidence::from_sample_size(4), Confidence::Low);\n323\t        assert_eq!(Confidence::from_sample_size(5), Confidence::Low);\n324\t        assert_eq!(Confidence::from_sample_size(14), Confidence::Low);\n325\t        assert_eq!(Confidence::from_sample_size(15), Confidence::Medium);\n326\t        assert_eq!(Confidence::from_sample_size(29), Confidence::Medium);\n327\t        assert_eq!(Confidence::from_sample_size(30), Confidence::High);\n328\t    }\n329\t\n330\t    #[test]\n331\t    fn }\n348\t}\n349\t"}]},"uuid":"5d52812d-3352-458d-a635-877840bc8ceb","timestamp":"2026-06-23T17:38:11.647Z","toolUseResult":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"/Users/jasonlee/Developer/maintenance/backend/crates/kernel/core/src/price_intel.rs","content":"//! Statistical price-intelligence primitives for the integrity engine.\n//!\n//! All functions operate on **sorted** or **unsorted** slices of `i64` amounts\n//! (won). They are pure — no I/O, no async — so they live in the kernel crate\n//! and can be called from any layer.\n//!\n//! ## Small-sample guard\n//!\n//! Statistical outlier flags are only reliable once a baseline of at least\n//! [`MIN_SAMPLE_SIZE`] peers exists. Below that threshold every function that\n//! would produce a false-precision score returns [`PriceIntelResult::Sparse`]\n//! instead of a numeric value. Callers that display this to users should show\n//! \"근거 부족 (데이터 부족)\" rather than any numeric flag.\n//!\n//! ## Confidence tiers\n//!\n//! | Sample size | Tier |\n//! |---|---|\n//! | < 5 | `Sparse` (no flag) |\n//! | 5–14 | `Low` |\n//! | 15–29 | `Medium` |\n//! | ≥ 30 | `High` |\n//!\n//! These thresholds are deliberately conservative. A false positive on a\n//! legitimate 기안 is more damaging to trust than missing a suspicious one.\n\n/// Minimum peer count required before any statistical outlier flag is issued.\npub const MIN_SAMPLE_SIZE: usize = 5;\n\n/// Confidence tier for a statistical finding.\n#[derive(\n    Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize,\n)]\n#[serde(rename_all = \"snake_case\")]\npub enum Confidence {\n    Low,\n    Medium,\n    High,\n}\n\nimpl Confidence {\n    #[must_use]\n    pub const fn from_sample_size(n: usize) -> Self {\n        if n >= 30 {\n            Self::High\n        } else if n >= 15 {\n            Self::Medium\n        } else {\n            Self::Low\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Result of a statistical outlier check.\n///\n/// [`Sparse`] means the sample is too small to produce a reliable signal.\n/// Callers should surface this as \"근거 부족 (데이터 부족)\", never as a flag.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize)]\n#[serde(rename_all = \"snake_case\", tag = \"kind\")]\npub enum PriceIntelResult {\n    /// Too few peers to compute a reliable statistic. Never produce a finding\n    /// from this — a false flag on scarce data harms legitimate users.\n    Sparse {\n        /// How many peers were available (for diagnostic display).\n        peer_count: usize,\n    },\n    /// The sample is large enough; here is the computed signal.\n    Computed {\n        /// Z-score of the target value against the peer distribution.\n        /// Positive = above the mean; negative = below.\n        z_score: f64,\n        /// Median absolute deviation (MAD) ratio: `|target - median| / MAD`.\n        /// More robust than z-score for small-to-medium skewed distributions.\n        /// `None` if MAD == 0 (all peers are identical).\n        mad_ratio: Option<f64>,\n        /// IQR fence check. `true` if `target > Q3 + 1.5 * IQR`.\n        above_iqr_fence: bool,\n        /// Percentile of the target value within the peer distribution (0–100).\n        percentile: f64,\n        /// Peer sample size (for confidence display).\n        peer_count: usize,\n        /// Statistical confidence tier.\n        confidence: Confidence,\n    },\n}\n\nimpl PriceIntelResult {\n    /// Returns `true` if the result is sparse (too few peers).\n    #[must_use]\n    pub const fn is_sparse(&self) -> bool {\n        matches!(self, Self::Sparse { .. })\n    }\n\n    /// Heuristic \"is this suspicious?\" check combining all signals.\n    ///\n    /// Returns `None` for sparse results (never flag).\n    /// For computed results, returns a score in [0.0, 1.0] where higher means\n    /// more suspicious. The caller maps this to a [`Severity`] threshold.\n    #[must_use]\n    pub fn suspicion_score(&self) -> Option<f64> {\n        match self {\n            Self::Sparse { .. } => None,\n            Self::Computed {\n                z_score,\n                mad_ratio,\n                above_iqr_fence,\n                percentile,\n                ..\n            } => {\n                // Weight the signals: z-score (normalized), MAD ratio, IQR fence,\n                // and raw percentile. All clamped to [0,1] before weighting.\n                let z_norm = (z_score.abs() / 4.0).min(1.0); // 4σ → max signal\n                let mad_norm = mad_ratio.map(|m| (m / 5.0).min(1.0)).unwrap_or(0.0); // 5× MAD → max signal\n                let iqr_signal = if *above_iqr_fence { 1.0 } else { 0.0 };\n                let pct_norm = ((*percentile - 90.0).max(0.0) / 10.0).min(1.0); // top 10% → max signal\n\n                // Only flag HIGH percentile (above average is normal; we want\n                // extreme outliers on the HIGH side — overpayment risk).\n                if *z_score < 0.0 {\n                    // Below mean — not a price-inflation concern.\n                    return Some(0.0);\n                }\n\n                let score = 0.35 * z_norm + 0.30 * mad_norm + 0.20 * iqr_signal + 0.15 * pct_norm;\n                Some(score.clamp(0.0, 1.0))\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Compute price-intelligence statistics for a target amount against a peer\n/// distribution.\n///\n/// # Arguments\n/// * `target` — the amount under scrutiny (i64 won).\n/// * `peers` — all amounts in the peer group INCLUDING `target` itself\n///   (the detector fetches the whole distribution, which naturally contains\n///   the row being checked). The function handles deduplication internally.\n///\n/// # Returns\n/// [`PriceIntelResult::Sparse`] if `peers.len() < MIN_SAMPLE_SIZE`, otherwise\n/// [`PriceIntelResult::Computed`] with full statistics.\n///\n/// # Panics\n/// Never. All arithmetic uses checked or finite-safe operations.\n#[must_use]\npub fn compute_price_intel(target: i64, peers: &[i64]) -> PriceIntelResult {\n    let n = peers.len();\n    if n < MIN_SAMPLE_SIZE {\n        return PriceIntelResult::Sparse { peer_count: n };\n    }\n\n    // Sort a copy for percentile / median / IQR.\n    let mut sorted = peers.to_vec();\n    sorted.sort_unstable();\n\n    let target_f = target as f64;\n    let n_f = n as f64;\n\n    // Mean and standard deviation.\n    let mean = sorted.iter().map(|&x| x as f64).sum::<f64>() / n_f;\n    let variance = sorted\n        .iter()\n        .map(|&x| {\n            let d = x as f64 - mean;\n            d * d\n        })\n        .sum::<f64>()\n        / n_f; // population variance (we have the full peer set, not a sample)\n    let std_dev = variance.sqrt();\n\n    let z_score = if std_dev > 0.0 {\n        (target_f - mean) / std_dev\n    } else {\n        0.0\n    };\n\n    // Median and MAD (median absolute deviation).\n    let median = percentile_sorted(&sorted, 50.0);\n    let deviations: Vec<f64> = sorted.iter().map(|&x| (x as f64 - median).abs()).collect();\n    let mad = {\n        let mut dev_sorted = deviations.clone();\n        dev_sorted.sort_by(f64::total_cmp);\n        percentile_f64_sorted(&dev_sorted, 50.0)\n    };\n    let mad_ratio = if mad > 0.0 {\n        Some((target_f - median).abs() / mad)\n    } else {\n        None\n    };\n\n    // IQR fence.\n    let q1 = percentile_sorted(&sorted, 25.0);\n    let q3 = percentile_sorted(&sorted, 75.0);\n    let iqr = q3 - q1;\n    let upper_fence = q3 + 1.5 * iqr;\n    let above_iqr_fence = target_f > upper_fence;\n\n    // Percentile of target.\n    let rank = sorted.partition_point(|&x| (x as f64) < target_f);\n    let percentile = if n == 1 {\n        50.0\n    } else {\n        (rank as f64) / ((n - 1) as f64) * 100.0\n    };\n\n    PriceIntelResult::Computed {\n        z_score,\n        mad_ratio,\n        above_iqr_fence,\n        percentile: percentile.clamp(0.0, 100.0),\n        peer_count: n,\n        confidence: Confidence::from_sample_size(n),\n    }\n}\n\n/// Compute the p-th percentile of a sorted `i64` slice using linear\n/// interpolation (nearest-rank with linear interpolation for non-integer\n/// positions).\n///\n/// `p` must be in `[0.0, 100.0]`. The slice must be non-empty and sorted.\n#[must_use]\nfn percentile_sorted(sorted: &[i64], p: f64) -> f64 {\n    debug_assert!(!sorted.is_empty());\n    debug_assert!((0.0..=100.0).contains(&p));\n\n    let n = sorted.len();\n    if n == 1 {\n        return sorted[0] as f64;\n    }\n\n    let index = p / 100.0 * (n as f64 - 1.0);\n    let lo = index.floor() as usize;\n    let hi = (lo + 1).min(n - 1);\n    let frac = index - lo as f64;\n\n    sorted[lo] as f64 * (1.0 - frac) + sorted[hi] as f64 * frac\n}\n\n/// Same as [`percentile_sorted`] but for `f64` slices (used for MAD\n/// computation).\n#[must_use]\nfn percentile_f64_sorted(sorted: &[f64], p: f64) -> f64 {\n    debug_assert!(!sorted.is_empty());\n\n    let n = sorted.len();\n    if n == 1 {\n        return sorted[0];\n    }\n\n    let index = p / 100.0 * (n as f64 - 1.0);\n    let lo = index.floor() as usize;\n    let hi = (lo + 1).min(n - 1);\n    let frac = index - lo as f64;\n\n    sorted[lo] * (1.0 - frac) + sorted[hi] * frac\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n\n    #[test]\n    fn sparse_below_min_sample() {\n        let result = compute_price_intel(100_000, &[100_000, 90_000, 80_000, 110_000]);\n        assert!(matches!(result, PriceIntelResult::Sparse { peer_count: 4 }));\n        assert!(result.is_sparse());\n        assert!(result.suspicion_score().is_none());\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn no_flag_for_below_mean() {\n        let peers: Vec<i64> = vec![100_000, 110_000, 105_000, 98_000, 102_000, 107_000, 99_000];\n        let result = compute_price_intel(80_000, &peers);\n        let score = result.suspicion_score().unwrap();\n        assert_eq!(score, 0.0, \"below-mean value should have zero suspicion\");\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn high_suspicion_for_extreme_outlier() {\n        // 10 normal peers, one extreme outlier target (10x the median).\n        let peers: Vec<i64> = vec![\n            100_000, 105_000, 98_000, 102_000, 110_000, 95_000, 108_000, 103_000, 99_000, 101_000,\n        ];\n        // Target is 10× the median.\n        let result = compute_price_intel(1_000_000, &peers);\n        match &result {\n            PriceIntelResult::Computed {\n                above_iqr_fence,\n                z_score,\n                ..\n            } => {\n                assert!(*above_iqr_fence, \"extreme value must be above IQR fence\");\n                assert!(*z_score > 2.0, \"z-score must be high for extreme outlier\");\n            }\n            PriceIntelResult::Sparse { .. } => panic!(\"should not be sparse\"),\n        }\n        let score = result.suspicion_score().unwrap();\n        assert!(\n            score > 0.5,\n            \"extreme outlier suspicion score should be high, got {score}\"\n        );\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn percentile_median_for_middle_value() {\n        let peers: Vec<i64> = (1..=11).map(|i| i * 10_000).collect();\n        let result = compute_price_intel(60_000, &peers);\n        if let PriceIntelResult::Computed { percentile, .. } = result {\n            // 60_000 is the exact median of 1..11 * 10_000.\n            assert!(\n                (percentile - 50.0).abs() < 1.0,\n                \"median value should be near 50th percentile, got {percentile}\"\n            );\n        } else {\n            panic!(\"expected Computed\");\n        }\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn confidence_tiers() {\n        assert_eq!(Confidence::from_sample_size(4), Confidence::Low);\n        assert_eq!(Confidence::from_sample_size(5), Confidence::Low);\n        assert_eq!(Confidence::from_sample_size(14), Confidence::Low);\n        assert_eq!(Confidence::from_sample_size(15), Confidence::Medium);\n        assert_eq!(Confidence::from_sample_size(29), Confidence::Medium);\n        assert_eq!(Confidence::from_sample_size(30), Confidence::High);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn uniform_distribution_no_mad_ratio() {\n        // All peers identical: MAD == 0, mad_ratio should be None.\n        let peers: Vec<i64> = vec![100_000; 6];\n        let result = compute_price_intel(100_000, &peers);\n        if let PriceIntelResult::Computed {\n            mad_ratio, z_score, ..\n        } = result\n        {\n            assert!(\n                mad_ratio.is_none(),\n                \"uniform peers must yield None mad_ratio\"\n            );\n            assert_eq!(z_score, 0.0, \"uniform peers must yield zero z-score\");\n        } else {\n            panic!(\"expected Computed for 6 identical peers\");\n        }\n    }\n}\n","numLines":349,"startLine":1,"totalLines":349}},"sourceToolAssistantUUID":"21f2b3a6-e780-4505-9dd3-90bdc07a34e9","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/jasonlee/Developer/maintenance","sessionId":"a4f6c1da-da69-4ccc-b409-be462b15706d","version":"2.1.185","gitBranch":"feat/multi-tenant-phase1","slug":"flickering-finding-valiant"}

period: Period,\n154\t    requested_scope: KpiScope,\n155\t    records: &[KpiInputRecord],\n156\t    inspection_records: &[KpiInspectionRecord],\n157\t    p1_records: &[KpiP1Record],\n158\t record,\n167\t        );\n168\t        add_record(\n169\t            &mut builders,\n170\t            KpiRollupScope::Branch(record.branch_id),\n171\t            record,\n172\t        );\n173\t      record,\n178\t            );\n179\t        }\n180\t    }\n181\t    for record in inspection_records {\n182\t        add_inspection_record(&mut builders, KpiRollupScope::Company, record);\n183\t        add_inspection_record(\n184\t            &mut builders,\n185\t            KpiRollupScope::Region(record.region_id),\n186\t            record,\n187\t        );\n188\t        add_inspection_record(\n189\t            &mut builders,\n190\t            KpiRollupScope::Branch(record.branch_id),\n191\t            record,\n192\t        );\n193\t        add_inspection_record(\n194\t            &mut builders,\n195\t            KpiRollupScope::Technician(record.technician_id),\n196\t            record,\n197\t        );\n198\t    }\n199\t    for record KpiRollupScope::Region(record.region_id),\n204\t            record,\n205\t        );\n206\t        add_p1_record(\n207\t            &mut builders,\n208\t            KpiRollupScope::Branch(record.branch_id),\n209\t            record,\n210\t        );\n211\t        if let Some(technician_id) = record.technician_id {\n212\t            add_p1_record(\n213\t                &mut builders,\n214\t                KpiRollupScope::Technician(technician_id),\n215\t                record,\n216\t            );\n217\t        }\n218\t    }\n219\t\n220\t    KpiReport {\n221\t        period,\n222\t        requested_scope,\n223\t        rollups: builders\n224\t            .into_iter()\n225\t            .map(|(scope, builder)| builder.finish(scope))\n226\t            .collect(),\n227\t        unavailable_metrics,\n228\t    }\n229\t}\n230\t\n231\tfn add_record(\n232\t    builders: &mut BTreeMap<KpiRollupScope, KpiRollupBuilder>,\n233\t    scope: {\n257\t    approved_report_count: u32,\n258\t    completed_count: u32,\n259\t    weighted_completed_points: u32,\n260\t    response_seconds_total: i128,\n261\t    response_count: u32,\n262\t    completion_seconds_total: i128,\n263\t    completion_count: u32,\n264\t    target_due_count: u32,\n265\t    target_due_compliant_count: u32,\n266\t    inspection_schedule_due_count: u32,\n267\t delay_reason_distribution: BTreeMap<String, u32>,\n273\t    work_order_ids: Vec<uuid::Uuid>,\n274\t}\n275\t\n276\timpl KpiRollupBuilder {\n277\t    fn push(&mut self, record: &KpiInputRecord) {\n278\t        self.approved_report_count += 1;\n279\t        self.work_order_ids.push(record.work_order_id);\n280\t\n281\t        if let Some(first_start) = record.first_in_progress_at\n282\t            && first_start >= record.created_at\n283\t        {\n284\t            self.response_seconds_total +=\n285\t                (first_start - record.created_at).whole_seconds() as i128;\n286\t            self.response_count += 1;\n287\t        }\n288\t\n289\t        if record.result_type == \"REVISIT_REQUIRED\" {\n290\t            self.revisit_count += 1;\n291\t        }\n292\t\n293\t        if let Some(reason) = record\n294\t            .delay_reason\n295\t            .as_ref()\n296\t            .filter(|reason| !reason.is_empty())\n297\t        {\n298\t            self.delay_count += 1;\n299\t            *self\n300\t                .delay_reason_distribution\n301\t                .entry(reason.clone())\n302\t                .or_insert(0) += 1;\n303\t        }\n304\t\n305\t        if !is_completed(record) {\n306\t            return;\n307\t        }\n308\t\n309\t        self.completed_count += 1;\n310\t        self.weighted_completed_points += priority_weight(&record.priority);\n311\t        if record.approved_at >= record.created_at {\n312\t            self.completion_seconds_total +=\n313\t                (record.approved_at - record.created_at).whole_seconds() as i128;\n314\t            self.completion_count += 1;\n315\t        }\n316\t        if let Some(target_due_at) = record.target_due_at {\n317\t            self.target_due_count += 1;\n318\t            if record.approved_at <= target_due_at {\n319\t                self.target_due_compliant_count += 1;\n320\t            }\n321\t        }\n322\t    }\n323\t\n324\t    fn push_inspection(&mut self, record: &KpiInspectionRecord) {\n325\t        self.inspection_schedule_due_count += 1;\n326\t        if record.completed {\n327\t            self.inspection_schedule_completed_count += 1;\n328\t        }\n329\t    }\n330\t\n331\t    fn push_p1(&mut self, record: &KpiP1Record) {\n332\t        self.p1_dispatch_count += 1;\n333\t        if record.accepted {\n334\t            self.p1_accepted_count += 1;\n335\t        }\n336\t    }\n337\t\n338\t    fn finish(mut self, scope: KpiRollupScope) -> KpiRollup {\n339\t        self.work_order_ids.sort_unstable();\n340\t        KpiRollup {\n341\t            scope,\n342\t            // Names are resolved by the adapter post-pass (DB lookup); the pure\n343\t            // domain calculation has no access to region/branch/user names.\n344\t            scope_display_name: None,\n345\t            approved_report_count: self.approved_report_count,\n346\t            completed_count: self.completed_count,\n347\t            weighted_completed_points: self.weighted_completed_points,\n348\t            inspection_schedule_due_count: self.inspection_schedule_due_count,\n349\t            inspection_schedule_completed_count: self.inspection_schedule_completed_count,\n350\t            inspection_plan_completion_bps: rate_bps(\n351\t                self.inspection_schedule_completed_count,\n352\t                self.inspection_schedule_due_count,\n353\t            ),\n354\t            p1_dispatch_count: self.p1_dispatch_count,\n355\t            p1_accepted_count: self.p1_accepted_count,\n356\t            p1_acceptance_bps: rate_bps(self.p1_accepted_count, self.p1_dispatch_count),\n357\t            average_response_seconds: average_i64(self.response_seconds_total, self.response_count),\n358\t            average_completion_seconds: average_i64(\n359\t                self.completion_seconds_total,\n360\t                self.completion_count,\n361\t            ),\n362\t            target_due_compliance_bps: rate_bps(\n363\t                self.target_due_compliant_count,\n364\t                self.target_due_count,\n365\t            ),\n366\t            revisit_rate_bps: rate_bps(self.revisit_count, self.approved_report_count).unwrap_or(0),\n367\t            delay_rate_bps: rate_bps(self.delay_count, self.approved_report_count).unwrap_or(0),\n368\t            delay_reason_distribution: self.delay_reason_distribution,\n369\t            work_order_ids: self.work_order_ids,\n370\t        }\n371\t    }\n372\t}\n373\t\n374\tfn is_completed(record: &KpiInputRecord) -> bool {\n375\t    record.status == \"FINAL_COMPLETED\"\n376\t}\n377\t\n378\tfn priority_weight(priority: &str) -> u32 {\n379\t    match priority {\n380\t        \"P1\" => 3,\n381\t        \"P2\" => 2,\n382\t        \"P3\" => 1,\n383\t        _ => 0,\n384\t    }\n385\t}\n386\t\n387\tfn average_i64(total: i128, count: u32) -> Option<i64> {\n388\t    if count == 0 {\n389\t        return None;\n390\t    }\n391\t    let count = i128::from(count);\n392\t    i64::try_from(total / count).ok()\n393\t}\n394\t\n395\tfn rate_bps(numerator: u32, denominator: u32) -> Option<u32> {\n396\t    numerator.saturating_mul(10_000).checked_div(denominator)\n397\t}\n398\t\n399\t#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n400\tpub struct ExportSourceNote {\n401\t    pub   }\n473\t    }\n474\t\n475\t    pub fn from_db_str(value: &str) -> Result<Self, mnt_kernel_core::KernelError> {\n476\t        match value {\n477\t            \"DRAFT\" => Ok(Self::Draft),\n478\t ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n499\t\n500\t/// One stage of the work-order funnel with its current open count.\n501\t///\n502\t/// `접수`/RECEIVED → `배정`/ASSIGNED → `진행`/IN_PROGRESS → `완료`/COMPLETED.\n503\t/// Counts are point-in-time (current `work_orders.status`), org-scoped by RLS.\n504\t#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, Serialize,   pub start: Timestamp,\n    #[serde(with = \"time::serde::rfc3339\")]\n    pub end: Timestamp,\n}\n\nimpl Period {\n    #[must_use]\n    pub fn contains(self, value: Timestamp) -> bool {\n        value >= self.start && value < self.end\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n#[serde(tag = \"kind\", content = \"id\", rename_all = \"snake_case\")]\npub Technician(UserId),\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, Hash, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n#[serde(rename_all = \"snake_case\")]\npub enum KpiMetric {\n    CompletedCount,\n    AverageResponseSpeed,\n    CompletionDurationAndDueCompliance,\n    RevisitRate,\n    DelayRateAndReasonDistribution,\n    InspectionPlanCompletionRate,\n    P1AcceptanceRate,\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct UnavailableMetric {\n    pub metric: KpiMetric,\n    pub source_domain: String,\n    pub reason: String,\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct KpiReport {\n    pub period: Period,\n    pub requested_scope: KpiScope,\n    pub rollups: Vec<KpiRollup>,\n    pub unavailable_metrics: Vec<UnavailableMetric>,\n}\n\nimpl KpiReport {\n    #[must_use]\n    pub fn rollup(&self, scope: &KpiRollupScope) -> Option<&KpiRollup> {\n        self.rollups.iter().find(|rollup| &rollup.scope == .find(|unavailable| unavailable.metric == metric)\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct KpiRollup {\n    pub scope: KpiRollupScope,\n    /// has no id) or a since-deleted\n    /// region/branch/user; the web renders it through `safeLabel` so a missing\n    /// name never leaks the UUID. `#[serde(default)]` keeps the pure domain\n    /// completed: bool,\n}\n\n/// One P1 emergency dispatch broadcast whose accept window opened within the\n/// reporting period. `accepted` is true when a mechanic accepted the broadcast\n/// (the dispatch reached `AUTO_ASSIGNED`, or at least one target responded\n/// `ACCEPT`) — i.e. the broadcast was answered without a manager force-assign.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]\npub struct KpiP1Record {\n    pub dispatch_id: uuid::Uuid,\n    pub branch_id: BranchId,\n    pub region_id: RegionId,\n    pub technician_id: Option<UserId>,\n    pub accepted: bool,\n}\n\n#[must_use]\npub fn calculate_kpi_report(\n    period: Period,\n    requested_scope: KpiScope,\n    records: &[KpiInputRecord],\n    inspection_records: &[KpiInspectionRecord],\n    p1_records: &[KpiP1Record],\n    unavailable_metrics: Vec<UnavailableMetric>,\n) -> KpiReport {\n    let mut builders = BTreeMap::<KpiRollupScope, KpiRollupBuilder>::new();\n    for record in records {\n        add_record(&mut builders, KpiRollupScope::Company, record);\n        add_record(\n            &mut builders,\n            KpiRollupScope::Region(record.region_id),\n            record,\n        );\n        add_record(\n            &mut builders,\n            KpiRollupScope::Branch(record.branch_id),\n            record,\n        );\n        if let Some(technician_id) = record.technician_id {\n            add_record(\n                &mut builders,\n                KpiRollupScope::Technician(technician_id),\n                record,\n            );\n        }\n    }\n    for record in inspection_records {\n        add_inspection_record(&mut builders, KpiRollupScope::Company, record);\n        add_inspection_record(\n            &mut builders,\n            KpiRollupScope::Region(record.region_id),\n            record,\n        );\n        add_inspection_record(\n            &mut builders,\n            KpiRollupScope::Branch(record.branch_id),\n            record,\n        );\n        add_inspection_record(\n            &mut builders,\n            KpiRollupScope::Technician(record.technician_id),\n            record,\n        );\n    }\n    for record in p1_records {\n        add_p1_record(&mut builders, KpiRollupScope::Company, record);\n        add_p1_record(\n            &mut builders,\n            KpiRollupScope::Region(record.region_id),\n            record,\n        );\n        add_p1_record(\n            &mut builders,\n            KpiRollupScope::Branch(record.branch_id),\n            record,\n        );\n        if let Some(technician_id) = record.technician_id {\n            add_p1_record(\n                &mut builders,\n                KpiRollupScope::Technician(technician_id),\n                record,\n            );\n        }\n    }\n\n    KpiReport {\n        period,\n        requested_scope,\n        rollups: builders\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|(scope, builder)| builder.finish(scope))\n            .collect(),\n        unavailable_metrics,\n    }\n}\n\nfn add_record(\n    builders: &mut BTreeMap<KpiRollupScope, KpiRollupBuilder>,\n    scope: KpiRollupScope,\n    record: &KpiInputRecord,\n) {\n    builders.entry(scope).or_default().push(record);\n}\n\nfn add_inspection_record(\n    builders: &mut BTreeMap<KpiRollupScope, KpiRollupBuilder>,\n    scope: KpiRollupScope,\n    record: &KpiInspectionRecord,\n) {\n    builders.entry(scope).or_default().push_inspection(record);\n}\n\nfn add_p1_record(\n    builders: &mut BTreeMap<KpiRollupScope, KpiRollupBuilder>,\n    scope: KpiRollupScope,\n    record: &KpiP1Record,\n) {\n    builders.entry(scope).or_default().push_p1(record);\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Default)]\nstruct KpiRollupBuilder {\n    approved_report_count: u32,\n    completed_count: u32,\n    weighted_completed_points: u32,\n    response_seconds_total: i128,\n    response_count: u32,\n    completion_seconds_total: i128,\n    completion_count: u32,\n    target_due_count: u32,\n    target_due_compliant_count: u32,\n    inspection_schedule_due_count: u32,\n    inspection_schedule_completed_count: u32,\n    p1_dispatch_count: u32,\n    p1_accepted_count: u32,\n    revisit_count: u32,\n    delay_count: u32,\n    delay_reason_distribution: BTreeMap<String, u32>,\n    work_order_ids: Vec<uuid::Uuid>,\n}\n\nimpl KpiRollupBuilder {\n    fn push(&mut self, record: &KpiInputRecord) {\n        self.approved_report_count += 1;\n        self.work_order_ids.push(record.work_order_id);\n\n        if let Some(first_start) = record.first_in_progress_at\n            && first_start >= record.created_at\n        {\n            self.response_seconds_total +=\n                (first_start - record.created_at).whole_seconds() as i128;\n            self.response_count += 1;\n        }\n\n        if record.result_type == \"REVISIT_REQUIRED\" {\n            self.revisit_count += 1;\n        }\n\n        if let Some(reason) = record\n            .delay_reason\n            .as_ref()\n            .filter(|reason| !reason.is_empty())\n        {\n            self.delay_count += 1;\n            *self\n                .delay_reason_distribution\n                .entry(reason.clone())\n                .or_insert(0) += 1;\n        }\n\n        if !is_completed(record) {\n            return;\n        }\n\n        self.completed_count += 1;\n        self.weighted_completed_points += priority_weight(&record.priority);\n        if record.approved_at >= record.created_at {\n            self.completion_seconds_total +=\n                (record.approved_at - record.created_at).whole_seconds() as i128;\n            self.completion_count += 1;\n        }\n        if let Some(target_due_at) = record.target_due_at {\n            self.target_due_count += 1;\n            if record.approved_at <= target_due_at {\n                self.target_due_compliant_count += 1;\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn push_inspection(&mut self, record: &KpiInspectionRecord) {\n        self.inspection_schedule_due_count += 1;\n        if record.completed {\n            self.inspection_schedule_completed_count += 1;\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn push_p1(&mut self, record: &KpiP1Record) {\n        self.p1_dispatch_count += 1;\n        if record.accepted {\n            self.p1_accepted_count += 1;\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn finish(mut self, scope: KpiRollupScope) -> KpiRollup {\n        self.work_order_ids.sort_unstable();\n        KpiRollup {\n            scope,\n            // Names are resolved by the adapter post-pass (DB lookup); the pure\n            // domain calculation has no access to region/branch/user names.\n            scope_display_name: None,\n            approved_report_count: self.approved_report_count,\n            completed_count: self.completed_count,\n            weighted_completed_points: self.weighted_completed_points,\n            inspection_schedule_due_count: self.inspection_schedule_due_count,\n            inspection_schedule_completed_count: self.inspection_schedule_completed_count,\n            inspection_plan_completion_bps: rate_bps(\n                self.inspection_schedule_completed_count,\n                self.inspection_schedule_due_count,\n            ),\n            p1_dispatch_count: self.p1_dispatch_count,\n            p1_accepted_count: self.p1_accepted_count,\n            p1_acceptance_bps: rate_bps(self.p1_accepted_count, self.p1_dispatch_count),\n            average_response_seconds: average_i64(self.response_seconds_total, self.response_count),\n            average_completion_seconds: average_i64(\n                self.completion_seconds_total,\n                self.completion_count,\n            ),\n            target_due_compliance_bps: rate_bps(\n                self.target_due_compliant_count,\n                self.target_due_count,\n            ),\n            revisit_rate_bps: rate_bps(self.revisit_count, self.approved_report_count).unwrap_or(0),\n            delay_rate_bps: rate_bps(self.delay_count, self.approved_report_count).unwrap_or(0),\n            delay_reason_distribution: self.delay_reason_distribution,\n            work_order_ids: self.work_order_ids,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nfn is_completed(record: &KpiInputRecord) -> bool {\n    record.status == \"FINAL_COMPLETED\"\n}\n\nfn priority_weight(priority: &str) -> u32 {\n    match priority {\n        \"P1\" => 3,\n        \"P2\" => 2,\n        \"P3\" => 1,\n        _ => 0,\n    }\n}\n\nfn average_i64(total: i128, count: u32) -> Option<i64> {\n    if count == 0 {\n        return None;\n    }\n    let count = i128::from(count);\n    i64::try_from(total / count).ok()\n}\n\nfn rate_bps(numerator: u32, denominator: u32) -> Option<u32> {\n    numerator.saturating_mul(10_000).checked_div(denominator)\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct ExportSourceNote {\n    pub source_domain: String,\n    pub Everything here is callable from any layer.\n\nuse mnt_kernel_core::{KernelError, OrgId, Timestamp, UserId};\nuse uuid::Uuid;\n\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// Finding severity and status\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n/// Severity of a governance finding. Maps to the `severity` CHECK column.\n#[derive(\n    Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize,\n)]\n#[serde(rename_all = \"SCREAMING_SNAKE_CASE\")]\npub enum FindingSeverity {\n    Info,\n    Low,\n    Medium,\n    High,\n    Critical,\n}\n\nimpl FindingSeverity {\n    #[must_use]\n    pub const fn as_db_str(self) -> &'static str {\n        match self {\n            Self::Info => \"INFO\",\n            Self::Low => \"LOW\",\n            Self::Medium => \"MEDIUM\",\n            Self::High => \"HIGH\",\n            Self::Critical => \"CRITICAL\",\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn from_db_str(value: &str) -> Result<Self, KernelError> {\n        match value {\n            \"INFO\" => Ok(Self::Info),\n            \"LOW\" => Ok(Self::Low),\n            \"MEDIUM\" => Ok(Self::Medium),\n            \"HIGH\" => Ok(Self::High),\n            \"CRITICAL\" => Ok(Self::Critical),\n            other => Err(KernelError::validation(format!(\n                \"unknown finding severity {other:?}\"\n            ))),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Map a suspicion score [0.0, 1.0] from `PriceIntelResult::suspicion_score`\n    /// to a severity level.\n    #[must_use]\n    pub fn from_suspicion_score(score: f64) -> Self {\n        if score >= 0.85 {\n            Self::Critical\n        } else if score >= 0.65 {\n            Self::High\n        } else if score >= 0.45 {\n            Self::Medium\n        } else if score >= 0.25 {\n            Self::Low\n        } else {\n            Self::Info\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Lifecycle status of a governance finding. Maps to the `status` CHECK column.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, Hash, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize)]\n#[serde(rename_all = \"SCREAMING_SNAKE_CASE\")]\npub enum FindingStatus {\n    Open,\n    Reviewed,\n    Dismissed,\n    Escalated,\n}\n\nimpl FindingStatus {\n    #[must_use]\n    pub const fn as_db_str(self) -> &'static str {\n        match self {\n            Self::Open => \"OPEN\",\n            Self::Reviewed => \"REVIEWED\",\n            Self::Dismissed => \"DISMISSED\",\n            Self::Escalated => \"ESCALATED\",\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn from_db_str(value: &str) -> Result<Self, KernelError> {\n        match value {\n            \"OPEN\" => Ok(Self::Open),\n            \"REVIEWED\" => Ok(Self::Reviewed),\n            \"DISMISSED\" => Ok(Self::Dismissed),\n            \"ESCALATED\" => Ok(Self::Escalated),\n            other => Err(KernelError::validation(format!(\n                \"unknown finding status {other:?}\"\n            ))),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// GovernanceFinding\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n/// A persisted governance finding as returned by list/detail queries.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize)]\npub struct GovernanceFinding {\n    pub id: Uuid,\n    pub org_id: OrgId,\n    pub detector_id: String,\n    pub entity_type: String,\n    pub entity_id: String,\n    pub source_audit_event_id: Option<Uuid>,\n    pub subject_user_id: Option<UserId>,\n    pub score: f64,\n    pub severity: FindingSeverity,\n    pub evidence: serde_json::Value,\n    pub status: FindingStatus,\n    #[serde(with = \"time::serde::rfc3339\")]\n    pub detected_at: Timestamp,\n    #[serde(with = \"time::serde::rfc3339\")]\n    pub created_at: Timestamp,\n    #[serde(with = \"time::serde::rfc3339\")]\n    pub updated_at: Timestamp,\n    pub reviewed_by: Option<UserId>,\n    #[serde(default, with = \"time::serde::rfc3339::option\")]\n    pub reviewed_at: Option<Timestamp>,\n    pub review_memo: Option<String>,\n}\n\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// Triage command\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n/// Valid target statuses for triage (OPEN → one of these).\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize)]\n#[serde(rename_all = \"SCREAMING_SNAKE_CASE\")]\npub enum TriageTarget {\n    Reviewed,\n    Dismissed,\n    Escalated,\n}\n\nimpl TriageTarget {\n    #[must_use]\n    pub const fn as_db_str(self) -> &'static str {\n        match self {\n            Self::Reviewed => \"REVIEWED\",\n            Self::Dismissed => \"DISMISSED\",\n            Self::Escalated => \"ESCALATED\",\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Command to triage (update the status of) a governance finding.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\npub struct TriageFindingCommand {\n    pub finding_id: Uuid,\n    pub reviewer: UserId,\n    pub new_status: TriageTarget,\n    /// Optional memo (max 2000 chars). Required for DISMISSED and ESCALATED.\n    pub memo: Option<String>,\n    pub occurred_at: Timestamp,\n    pub trace: mnt_kernel_core::TraceContext,\n}\n\n/// Validate a triage memo: required for DISMISSED/ESCALATED, optional for REVIEWED.\n/// Max 2000 chars (mirrors DB CHECK).\npub fn validate_triage_memo(\n    target: TriageTarget,\n    memo: &Option<String>,\n) -> Result<(), KernelError> {\n    match memo {\n        Some(m) if m.trim().is_empty() => {\n            Err(KernelError::validation(\"review_memo must not be blank\"))\n        }\n        Some(m) if m.len() > 2000 => Err(KernelError::validation(\n            \"review_memo must not exceed 2000 characters\",\n        )),\n        None if matches!(target, TriageTarget::Dismissed | TriageTarget::Escalated) => {\n            Err(KernelError::validation(\n                \"review_memo is required when dismissing or escalating a finding\",\n            ))\n        }\n        _ => Ok(()),\n    }\n}\n\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// Detector trait\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n/// A governance detector. Detectors are called OnWrite (cheap) or in batch.\n///\n/// The trait is pure: it takes context and returns a finding payload.\n/// The caller is responsible for persisting the result to `governance_findings`.\npub trait Detector: Send + Sync {\n    /// Dot-namespaced detector identifier, e.g. `\"integrity.price_outlier\"`.\n    fn detector_id(&self) -> &'static str;\n}\n\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// Price-outlier detector output\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n/// The result of running the price-outlier detector on a single purchase request.\n/// The caller (store layer) decides whether to persist this as a finding.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize)]\npub struct PriceOutlierOutput {\n    pub detector_id: &'static str,\n    pub entity_type: &'static str,\n    pub entity_id: String,\n    pub score: f64,\n    pub severity: FindingSeverity,\n    /// The full `PriceIntelResult` evidence, serialised as JSON.\n    pub evidence: serde_json::Value,\n    /// `true` if the result is sparse (too few peers) — caller should NOT persist.\n    pub is_sparse: bool,\n}\n\n/// Run the price-outlier detector for a single purchase amount against the\n/// `peers` distribution for its (vendor, category) bucket.\n///\n/// Returns `None` if `is_sparse` — no finding should be persisted.\n///\n/// This is a pure function callable from any layer.\n#[must_use]\npub fn run_price_outlier_detector(\n    purchase_request_id: uuid::Uuid,\n    amount_won: i64,\n    peers: &[i64],\n) -> PriceOutlierOutput {\n    use mnt_kernel_core::compute_price_intel;\n\n    let result = compute_price_intel(amount_won, peers);\n    let is_sparse = result.is_sparse();\n    let score = result.suspicion_score().unwrap_or(0.0);\n    let severity = FindingSeverity::from_suspicion_score(score);\n\n    let evidence = serde_json::to_value(&result).unwrap_or(serde_json::Value::Null);\n\n    PriceOutlierOutput {\n        detector_id: \"anomaly.price_outlier\",\n        entity_type: \"financial_purchase_request\",\n        entity_id: purchase_request_id.to_string(),\n        score,\n        severity,\n        evidence,\n        is_sparse,\n    }\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n\n    #[test]\n    fn severity_roundtrip() {\n        for sev in [\n            FindingSeverity::Info,\n            FindingSeverity::Low,\n            FindingSeverity::Medium,\n            FindingSeverity::High,\n            FindingSeverity::Critical,\n        ] {\n            assert_eq!(FindingSeverity::from_db_str(sev.as_db_str()).unwrap(), sev);\n        }\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn status_roundtrip() {\n        for status in [\n            FindingStatus::Open,\n            FindingStatus::Reviewed,\n            FindingStatus::Dismissed,\n            FindingStatus::Escalated,\n        ] {\n            assert_eq!(\n                FindingStatus::from_db_str(status.as_db_str()).unwrap(),\n                status\n            );\n        }\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn severity_from_score() {\n        assert_eq!(\n            FindingSeverity::from_suspicion_score(0.0),\n            FindingSeverity::Info\n        );\n        assert_eq!(\n            FindingSeverity::from_suspicion_score(0.25),\n            FindingSeverity::Low\n        );\n        assert_eq!(\n            FindingSeverity::from_suspicion_score(0.45),\n            FindingSeverity::Medium\n        );\n        assert_eq!(\n            FindingSeverity::from_suspicion_score(0.65),\n            FindingSeverity::High\n        );\n        assert_eq!(\n            FindingSeverity::from_suspicion_score(0.85),\n            FindingSeverity::Critical\n        );\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn triage_memo_validation() {\n        // Reviewed: memo optional.\n        assert!(validate_triage_memo(TriageTarget::Reviewed, &None).is_ok());\n        // Dismissed: memo required.\n        assert!(validate_triage_memo(TriageTarget::Dismissed, &None).is_err());\n        assert!(validate_triage_memo(TriageTarget::Dismissed, &Some(\"valid memo\".into())).is_ok());\n        // Blank memo rejected.\n        assert!(validate_triage_memo(TriageTarget::Reviewed, &Some(\"   \".into())).is_err());\n        // Too long.\n        let long = \"x\".repeat(2001);\n        assert!(validate_triage_memo(TriageTarget::Reviewed, &Some(long)).is_err());\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn price_outlier_sparse_below_min_sample() {\n        let peers: Vec<i64> = vec![100_000, 90_000, 80_000];\n        let out = run_price_outlier_detector(uuid::Uuid::new_v4(), 200_000, &peers);\n        assert!(out.is_sparse, \"should be sparse with 3 peers\");\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn price_outlier_detects_extreme_value() {\n        let peers: Vec<i64> = (0..10).map(|i| 100_000 + i * 1_000).collect();\n        // 10x the median is a clear outlier.\n        let out = run_price_outlier_detector(uuid::Uuid::new_v4(), 1_000_000, &peers);\n        assert!(!out.is_sparse);\n        assert!(\n            out.score > 0.5,\n So `(returned_at - assigned_at)` per source equipment is a **directly available downtime proxy** for availability/uptime calculations — even though there's no dedicated downtime field on work orders. This is a key roadmap finding: equipment availability is computable today without new schema.\n\nI now have all the codebase grounding I need.
