{"parentUuid":"bc43c7ef-1118-4ad6-a963-aa7c322e2484","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"94931824-5fbc-4694-a614-3c3c4af72979","agentId":"a1fb0fb2cb5fa37d4","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":"[SYSTEM NOTIFICATION - NOT USER INPUT]\nThis is an automated background-task event, NOT a message from the user.\nDo NOT interpret this as user acknowledgement, confirmation, or response to any pending question.\n\n<task-notification>\n<task-id>a44b7ed890a25a1af</task-id>\n<tool-use-id>toolu_01LDX1BHkjEwqoWEUG6tRbhz</tool-use-id>\n<output-file>/private/tmp/claude-501/-Users-jasonlee-Developer-maintenance/c5cc817d-9c43-450f-8df3-1995ed2ea4f0/tasks/a44b7ed890a25a1af.output</output-file>\n<status>completed</status>\n<summary>Agent \"Research FSM/CMMS analytics best practices\" came to rest</summary>\n<note>A task-notification fires each time this agent comes to rest with no live background children of its own. The user can send it another message and resume it, so the same task-id may notify more than once.</note>\n<result>I have all the data needed. Here is the full research report.\n\n---\n\n## Research: Maintenance &amp; Field-Service Analytics — Best-Practice KPIs, Benchmarks, and Tool Dashboards\n\n---\n\n## Category 1: Core Maintenance / Reliability KPIs\n\n### 1.1 MTBF — Mean Time Between Failures\n\n- **Definition:** The average operating time between consecutive failures on a repairable asset.\n- **Formula:** `MTBF = Total Operational Uptime / Number of Failures`\n- **Benchmark:** No single universal number; for heavy rotating equipment a healthy MTBF is 400–800 hours; for excavators world-class is &gt;800 hours (industry average 400–600 h); for industrial conveyor motors ≥4,000 hours is considered reliable. World-class organizations on critical equipment achieve availability of 99%+ which implies MTBF &gt;&gt; MTTR.\n- **Sources:** [f7i.ai MTTR/MTBF Playbook](https://f7i.ai/blog/mttr-and-mtbf-the-maintenance-leaders-strategic-playbook-for-2025) | [oxmaint KPIs Guide](https://oxmaint.com/article/mtbf-mttr-oee-maintenance-kpis)\n\n---\n\n### 1.2 MTTR — Four Variants (critical distinction)\n\nAll four share the abbreviation MTTR but measure different spans:\n\n| Variant | Span measured | Formula |\n|---|---|---|\n| **Mean Time to Respond** | First alert → first qualified technician action | `Total response time / Number of incidents` |\n| **Mean Time to Repair** | Hands-on wrench time only; excludes wait, travel, parts logistics | `Active repair time / Number of repairs` |\n| **Mean Time to Recover** | Failure onset → full operational restoration (detection + response + repair + verification) | `Total restoration time / Number of incidents` |\n| **Mean Time to Resolve** | Failure → permanent fix confirmed; longest of the four | `Time to permanent fix / Number of incidents` |\n\nOrder of magnitude: Respond ≤ Repair ≤ Recover ≤ Resolve.\n\n- **Benchmark:** For manufacturing equipment: world-class MTTR (Repair) &lt; 6 hours; industry average 12–18 hours. Field service target: same-day or next-business-day.\n- **Sources:** [Causely — The \"R\" in MTTR](https://www.causely.ai/blog/mttr-meaning) | [BetterStack MTTR Variants](https://betterstack.com/community/guides/incident-management/mttr-and-other-incident-metrics/) | [Splunk MTTR](https://www.splunk.com/en_us/blog/learn/mttr-mean-time-to-repair.html) | [oxmaint Benchmarks](https://oxmaint.com/article/mtbf-mttr-oee-maintenance-kpis)\n\n---\n\n### 1.3 Equipment Availability / Uptime / OEE\n\n**Equipment Availability (mechanical availability):**\n- **Definition:** Percentage of scheduled time an asset is operational and ready to work.\n- **Formula:** `Availability = MTBF / (MTBF + MTTR)` or `Uptime / (Uptime + Downtime) × 100`\n- **Benchmark:** World-class &gt;92%; industry average 72–78%. (Nakajima OEE framework component target: 90%.)\n- **Source:** [oxmaint OEE Guide](https://oxmaint.com/industries/manufacturing-plant/oee-calculation-formula-benchmark-manufacturing-improvement-strategies)\n\n**OEE — Overall Equipment Effectiveness:**\n- **Definition:** Single composite score of how productively equipment is running against its theoretical maximum.\n- **Formula:** `OEE = Availability × Performance × Quality` (each as a decimal)\n  - Availability = Run Time / Planned Production Time\n  - Performance = (Ideal Cycle Time × Total Count) / Run Time\n  - Quality = Good Count / Total Count\n- **Nakajima world-class component targets:** Availability 90%, Performance 95%, Quality 99% → OEE = 0.90 × 0.95 × 0.99 = **84.6% ≈ 85%**\n- **Benchmark:** 85% OEE = world-class; industry average 60–65%.\n- **Sources:** [leanproduction.com OEE](https://www.leanproduction.com/oee/) | [symestic OEE](https://www.symestic.com/en-us/blog/oee) | [eMaint OEE](https://www.emaint.com/oee-calculation/) | [oxmaint OEE](https://oxmaint.com/industries/manufacturing-plant/oee-calculation-formula-benchmark-manufacturing-improvement-strategies)\n\n---\n\n### 1.4 Planned vs. Unplanned Maintenance Ratio (PMP)\n\n- **Definition:** Percentage of total maintenance hours that are planned/scheduled vs. reactive/emergency.\n- **Formula:** `PMP = (Planned Maintenance Hours / Total Maintenance Hours) × 100`\n- **Benchmark:**\n  - World-class target: **80–90% planned** (20–10% reactive) — the \"80/20 rule\"\n  - Manufacturing targets: 85/15; Utilities: 90/10\n  - Industry average: 50–65% planned (reactive organizations: 36% planned)\n- **Source:** [Limble Planned vs Unplanned](https://limble.com/blog/planned-vs-unplanned-maintenance-ratio) | [MaintainX PMP Learning Center](https://www.getmaintainx.com/learning-center/planned-maintenance-percentage) | [Tractian PMP Glossary](https://tractian.com/en/glossary/planned-maintenance-percentage)\n\n---\n\n### 1.5 PM Compliance / PM Completion Rate\n\n- **Definition:** Percentage of scheduled preventive maintenance tasks completed on time within the compliance window.\n- **Formula:** `PMC = (# Completed PMs / # Scheduled PMs) × 100`\n  - Industry applies the **10% Rule**: a PM is \"on time\" if completed within ±10% of its interval (e.g., a 30-day PM is compliant if done between day 27–33).\n- **Benchmark:** World-class = **90%+**; strong operating range = 85–95%; below 70% signals reactive takeover; below 80% = program not functioning.\n- **Sources:** [Fiix PM Compliance Metric](https://fiixsoftware.com/maintenance-metrics/preventive-maintenance-compliance/) | [MaintainX PM Compliance Blog](https://www.getmaintainx.com/blog/preventive-maintenance-pm-compliance) | [SMRP Best Practices 6th Ed., cited via Fiix]\n\n---\n\n### 1.6 Schedule Compliance and Maintenance Backlog\n\n**Schedule Compliance:**\n- **Definition:** Percentage of planned maintenance tasks (PM + predictive) actually executed on schedule.\n- **Formula:** `Schedule Compliance = (Tasks Completed on Schedule / Tasks Scheduled) × 100`\n- **Benchmark:** World-class = **90%+**; industry average = 60–70%.\n\n**Maintenance Backlog:**\n- **Definition:** Total volume of planned maintenance work not yet completed, expressed in technician-weeks.\n- **Benchmark:** Healthy = **2–4 weeks** per technician; below 2 weeks = planners cannot build efficient schedules; above 6 weeks = equipment risk is accumulating (deferred maintenance compounds ~7% annually).\n- **Sources:** [reliamag.com KPIs](https://reliamag.com/articles/maintenance-kpis-that-actually-matter/) | [Tractian 8 KPIs Guide](https://tractian.com/en/blog/8-kpis-for-maintenance-management) | [UpKeep CMMS KPI Benchmarks](https://upkeep.com/learning/cmms-maintenance-kpi-benchmarks/)\n\n---\n\n### 1.7 Maintenance Cost as % of RAV (MC/RAV)\n\n- **Definition:** Annual total maintenance spend divided by the current replacement cost of all physical assets, expressed as a percentage. The primary asset-management financial benchmark from SMRP.\n- **Formula:** `MC/RAV (%) = (Annual Maintenance Cost / Replacement Asset Value) × 100`\n- **Benchmark (SMRP Best Practices 6th Edition, 2020):**\n\n| Industry | Typical Range | World-Class Target |\n|---|---|---|\n| Chemical &amp; Process | 2–4% | &lt; 2% |\n| Food &amp; Beverage | 2–5% | &lt; 2.5% |\n| Power / Utilities | 2–5% | &lt; 2.5% |\n| General Manufacturing | 2–5% | 2–2.5% |\n| Mining &amp; Metals | 3–6% | 2.5–3% |\n| Oil &amp; Gas | 3–7% | &lt; 3.5% |\n| Facility Management | 1.5–4% | &lt; 2% |\n\n  Widely-cited cross-industry world-class target: **2–3% of RAV.**\n  SMRP caution: a low MC/RAV may indicate under-maintenance, not excellence.\n- **Sources:** [Fiix MC/RAV Metric](https://fiixsoftware.com/maintenance-metrics/mcrav/) | [Tractian RAV Blog](https://tractian.com/en/blog/replacement-asset-value-rav-what-is-it) | [MaintainX RAV Guide](https://www.getmaintainx.com/blog/replacement-asset-value) | SMRP Best Practices, 6th Ed.\n\n---\n\n## Category 2: Field-Service-Specific KPIs\n\n### 2.1 First-Time Fix Rate (FTFR)\n\n- **Definition:** Percentage of service jobs resolved completely on the first technician visit, requiring no return trip.\n- **Formula:** `FTFR = (Jobs Fixed on First Visit / Total Service Jobs) × 100`\n- **Benchmark:**\n  - Industry average: **75–80%** (2024 Field Service Benchmark Report: 76%; Aberdeen Group: ~75%)\n  - Top 20% of organizations: 88%+\n  - Bottom 20%: 55%\n  - Target / ideal: **90%**; below 70% = systemic problem\n  - Industrial Machinery segment: 71.9%; Food Equipment: 79.8%\n- **Sources:** [2024 Field Service Benchmark Report (HubSpot PDF)](https://21176235.fs1.hubspotusercontent-na1.net/hubfs/21176235/ebook-2024-benchmarkreport-12-19.pdf) | [IBM FTFR](https://www.ibm.com/think/topics/first-time-fix-rate) | [PTC FTFR](https://www.ptc.com/en/blogs/service/what-is-first-time-fix-rate) | [ServiceTitan Field Service Metrics](https://www.servicetitan.com/blog/field-service-metrics)\n\n---\n\n### 2.2 Mean Time to Respond / SLA Compliance\n\n- **Definition (Mean Time to Respond):** Average elapsed time from when a service request is received to when the first qualified technician acknowledges and begins action.\n- **Formula:** `MTTRespond = Total Response Time Across All Calls / Number of Calls`\n- **Definition (SLA Compliance Rate):** Percentage of service calls where response (and/or resolution) occurs within the contractually committed time window.\n- **Formula:** `SLA Compliance = (# Calls Met within SLA / Total Calls) × 100`\n- **Benchmark:** SLA compliance target: **95%+** for customer-facing agreements; response time SLAs for heavy equipment typically 2–4 hours for critical, 8–24 hours for standard.\n- **Sources:** [ServiceTitan Field Service Metrics](https://www.servicetitan.com/blog/field-service-metrics) | [2024 Field Service Benchmark Report](https://21176235.fs1.hubspotusercontent-na1.net/hubfs/21176235/ebook-2024-benchmarkreport-12-19.pdf)\n\n---\n\n### 2.3 Technician Utilization / Wrench Time\n\n**Technician Utilization (Billable Hours):**\n- **Definition:** Percentage of a technician's paid shift hours spent on revenue-generating / productive customer work.\n- **Formula:** `Utilization = (Billable / Productive Hours / Total Available Hours) × 100`\n- **Benchmark:** 60–80% is strong; 65–80% is a realistic and sustainable target; above 85% = overbooked / quality risk. Industry average: 55–60%.\n\n**Wrench Time (active hands-on time only):**\n- **Definition:** Narrower than utilization — only the share of a shift spent physically working on equipment, excluding travel, parts collection, admin, and waiting.\n- **Benchmark:** Industry typical wrench time: **25–35%** of shift. HVAC with optimized dispatch: 60–65%. Maintenance technicians in structured environments can reach 40–50% wrench time.\n- **Sources:** [FieldEdge Technician Utilization Benchmarks](https://fieldedge.com/blog/technician-utilization-benchmarks/) | [aiventic FSM Glossary](https://www.aiventic.ai/the-ultimate-glossary-for-field-service-management/technician-utilization) | [The Certify Hub — Wrench Time](https://thecertifyhub.com/wrenchtime/) | [ServiceTitan Field Service Metrics](https://www.servicetitan.com/blog/field-service-metrics)\n\n---\n\n### 2.4 Mean Time to Complete / Jobs Per Tech Per Day\n\n**Mean Time to Complete:**\n- **Definition:** Average elapsed time from initial dispatch call through job completion (service + billing).\n- **Benchmark:** Simple tasks: 1–2 hours; installations/full-day projects: 6–8 hours.\n\n**Jobs per Technician per Day:**\n- **Definition:** Average number of distinct service jobs completed by one tech in a working day.\n- **Benchmark:** Standard: **3–5 jobs/day**; high-volume service (short jobs): up to 7 jobs/day depending on service type.\n- **Source:** [ServiceTitan Field Service Metrics](https://www.servicetitan.com/blog/field-service-metrics)\n\n---\n\n### 2.5 Customer Satisfaction / NPS in Field Service\n\n**CSAT:**\n- **Definition:** Post-job satisfaction score, typically 1–5 star survey.\n- **Benchmark:** Good CSAT range = 70–90%.\n- **Source:** [ServiceTitan Field Service Metrics](https://www.servicetitan.com/blog/field-service-metrics)\n\n**NPS (Net Promoter Score):**\n- **Definition:** Measures customer loyalty. Promoters (score 9–10) minus Detractors (score 0–6), expressed as a number from -100 to +100.\n- **Formula:** `NPS = % Promoters − % Detractors`\n- **Benchmark:** HVAC / field service: NPS above **50 is excellent**, above 70 is world-class. Global B2C average: 49 (Retently 2025). Telecom (comparable service): average 19.\n- **Sources:** [Retently NPS Benchmark Report 2025](https://www.retently.com/blog/good-net-promoter-score/) | [Trustmary NPS by Industry](https://trustmary.com/nps-net-promoter-score/nps-by-industry/) | [HVAC KPIs — jbwarranties](https://blog.jbwarranties.com/key-performance-indicators-for-hvac-companies)\n\n---\n\n## Category 3: Asset-Management / Financial Intelligence\n\n### 3.1 Maintenance Cost Per Asset / Cost Trend\n\n- **Definition:** Total annual maintenance spend allocated to a specific asset or asset class; tracked over time to identify cost drift.\n- **Formula:** `Cost per Asset = Total Maintenance Spend on Asset / Number of Assets (or per unit of output)`\n- **Benchmark:** Specific to asset type; tracked as a trend (month-over-month, year-over-year). Paired with MC/RAV for context.\n- **Source:** [Limble Analytics Features](https://limble.com/products/reports-dashboards/) | [UpKeep Analytics](https://upkeep.com/product/analytics-reporting/)\n\n---\n\n### 3.2 Repair vs. Replace / TCO Analysis\n\n- **Definition:** A decision framework comparing the cost of repairing an aging asset against replacing it, using lifecycle cost analysis (LCA) and total cost of ownership (TCO).\n- **Common Rule-of-Thumb Thresholds:**\n  - **50% Rule (most widely used in industrial asset management):** If the cost of a repair exceeds 50% of the asset's current replacement value, replacement is the financially sounder decision. Widely applied because aging assets have compounding risk of repeat failures within 12–24 months.\n  - **65% Rule (US Marine Corps / Army Regulation 750-1):** Economic repair = repair cost ≤ 65% of replacement unit price.\n  - **75% Rule (general industry standard):** If repair + maintenance costs exceed 75% of replacement cost, replace.\n  - For assets &gt;$50,000 replacement value, a rigorous NPV comparison is recommended rather than a rule of thumb.\n- **Sources:** [Maintainly 75% Rule Article](https://maintainly.com/articles/understanding-the-75-maintenance-rule-in-asset-management-when-to-repair-or-replace) | [Art of Troubleshooting — 50% Rule](https://artoftroubleshooting.com/2014/04/25/the-50-percent-rule-repair-or-replace-revisited/) | [Reliabilityweb Repair vs Replace (LCA)](https://reliabilityweb.com/articles/entry/repair-versus-replace-how-to-use-lifecycle-cost-analysis-to-determine-the-t) | [WARU Acquipedia](https://www.waru.edu/acquipedia-article/repair-vs-replacement-decision-making)\n\n---\n\n### 3.3 Rental / Asset Utilization Rate and ROI\n\n**Time Utilization:**\n- **Definition:** Percentage of available fleet time (or equipment units) actually on rent.\n- **Formula:** `Time Utilization = (Units on Rent / Total Fleet Units) × 100`\n- **Benchmark:** **65–75%** overall is healthy; industry standard: 72% out on rent, 20% in yard and rental-ready, ≤8% non-rental-ready. Below 60% = excess idle inventory; above 85% = stockout risk.\n\n**Dollar / Financial Utilization:**\n- **Definition:** Annual rental revenue generated by an asset as a percentage of its acquisition cost (or all equipment expenses + debt).\n- **Benchmark:** National enterprises: ~65%; small local operators: ~100%. Leading rental companies achieve EBITDA margins of **40%+**.\n\n**ROI / Profitability:**\n- **Benchmark:** Net profit margins: top performers 15–25%; average operators 8–12%. Break-even target: **12–24 months** per asset. Income-to-maintenance ratio target: maintenance ≤ **15–20% of rental revenue**.\n- **Sources:** [Quipli Equipment Rental KPIs](https://quipli.com/resources/top-kpis-for-a-rental-business/) | [Hapn Fleet Utilization Benchmarks 2026](https://gethapn.com/blog/fleet-utilization-benchmarks-2026-is-your-equipment-actually-making-money/) | [InTempo — Time vs Dollar Utilization](https://www.intemposoftware.com/blog/equipment-rental-metrics-time-dollar-utilization) | [Dealstream Rental Benchmarks](https://dealstream.com/industry-guides/equipment-rental-businesses/rules-of-thumb)\n\n---\n\n### 3.4 Parts / Inventory Spend — MRO Inventory Turns\n\n- **Definition:** Number of times the MRO (maintenance, repair, and operations) spare-parts inventory is consumed and replenished per year. Unlike retail, higher is not always better — critical insurance spares are intentionally slow-moving.\n- **Formula:** `Inventory Turns = Annual Parts Cost of Goods Used / Average Inventory Value`\n- **Benchmark:**\n  - General MRO consumables: **1.0–3.0 turns/year** is healthy.\n  - Food &amp; Beverage: 2.5–4.0 turns/year.\n  - Power plant critical spares: 0.5–1.5 turns/year (intentionally low).\n  - Critical insurance spares: 0.5 or lower is acceptable.\n  - MRO inventory commonly accounts for **40–50% of total maintenance budget** in manufacturing.\n  - 15–25% of MRO inventory at most facilities is obsolete or surplus.\n- **Sources:** [f7i.ai MRO Inventory Turns 2026](https://f7i.ai/blog/inventory-turns-in-mro-the-definitive-guide-to-optimizing-spare-parts-in-2026) | [f7i.ai Inventory Turnover Guide](https://f7i.ai/blog/what-is-inventory-turnover-the-definitive-guide-to-mro-inventory-metrics-in-2026) | [UpKeep MRO Parts Inventory](https://upkeep.com/learning/mro-parts-inventory/)\n\n---\n\n## Category 4: Predictive &amp; Advanced Intelligence\n\n### 4.1 Predictive Maintenance Signals\n\n**Vibration Analysis (most common for rotating equipment):**\n- **Definition:** Condition-based technique that monitors the vibration signature of rotating assets (motors, pumps, compressors, gearboxes, fans, bearings). Every healthy asset has a unique baseline signature; degradation changes that signature before visible/audible symptoms appear.\n- **How it works:** Accelerometers collect raw time-waveform data → Fast Fourier Transform (FFT) converts to frequency spectrum → deviations from baseline indicate imbalance, misalignment, bearing wear, looseness, etc.\n- **Detection lead time:** Vibration faults can be detected weeks to months before failure.\n- **Sources:** [Fluke Vibration for PdM](https://www.fluke.com/en-us/learn/blog/vibration/measuring-vibration-for-predictive-maintenance) | [MaintainX Vibration Analysis](https://www.getmaintainx.com/learning-center/using-vibration-analysis-in-predictive-maintenance) | [Tractian Vibration Sensors](https://tractian.com/en/blog/vibration-sensor-predictive-maintenance)\n\n**Usage/Hours-Based Triggers:**\n- Service intervals triggered by accumulated engine hours, cycles, mileage, or operating hours rather than calendar time — directly relevant to forklifts and heavy equipment. Standard forklift PM intervals: every 250–500 operating hours.\n\n**Other Condition Monitoring Signals:**\n- Oil analysis (particle count, viscosity, contamination) — detects internal wear.\n- Thermal imaging / IR — detects electrical hot spots, bearing friction, insulation failure.\n- Ultrasound — detects compressed air leaks, early bearing defects, electrical arcing.\n- Current/power monitoring — motor health and efficiency degradation.\n\n**Sources:** [Banner Engineering — Vibration Monitoring for PdM](https://www.bannerengineering.com/us/en/solutions/iiot-data-driven-factory/vibration-monitoring-for-predictive-maintenance.html) | [Tractian Vibration Sensor PdM](https://tractian.com/en/blog/vibration-sensor-predictive-maintenance) | [NCD.io PdM Starter Guide](https://ncd.io/blog/predictive-maintenance-with-vibration-sensors-the-complete-starter-guide/)\n\n---\n\n### 4.2 Failure / Root-Cause / Pareto Analysis — Bad-Actor Identification\n\n- **The Pareto Principle in Maintenance (80/20 Rule):** In virtually every CMMS dataset, **20% of assets** (or 20% of failure modes) account for **80% of total downtime, work orders, and maintenance cost**. These are \"bad actor\" assets.\n- **Bad-Actor Definition:** A piece of equipment that fails more frequently than average, generating disproportionate costs and production interruptions.\n- **Bad-Actor Identification Process:**\n  1. Export all corrective work orders from CMMS over a 12-month window.\n  2. Rank assets by (a) failure frequency and (b) total maintenance cost.\n  3. Pareto-chart: the top 20% of assets driving 80% of cost/downtime are bad actors.\n  4. Apply RCA (Root Cause Analysis — e.g., 5-Whys, Fishbone/Ishikawa, FMEA) to each bad actor.\n- **Key data quality requirement:** Failure codes must be consistently used; \"Unknown/Other\" in &gt;40% of work orders makes Pareto analysis unreliable.\n- **Sources:** [f7i.ai Pareto Analysis in Maintenance](https://f7i.ai/blog/pareto-analysis-in-maintenance-the-definitive-guide-to-the-8020-rule-for-industrial-reliability) | [Reliabilityweb Bad Actor Program](https://reliabilityweb.com/articles/entry/bad-actor-program) | [Fabrico.io CMMS for Bad Actor Assets](https://www.fabrico.io/blog/cmms-software-identify-bad-actor-assets-manufacturing/) | [oxmaint Downtime Pareto Analysis](https://oxmaint.com/industries/manufacturing-plant/downtime-pareto-analysis-for-plant-maintenance-leaders)\n\n---\n\n### 4.3 Anomaly Detection in Maintenance Data\n\n- **Definition:** Machine-learning algorithms that establish a statistical baseline of \"normal\" sensor readings (vibration, temperature, current, pressure) and automatically flag deviations that exceed learned thresholds.\n- **How it differs from threshold alerting:** Traditional alerting fires when a hard limit is crossed (e.g., temp &gt; 90°C). ML anomaly detection fires when the pattern deviates from the learned norm even if absolute values are still in spec — enabling earlier detection.\n- **IBM Maximo Monitor specifically:** Uses AI/ML anomaly detection on IoT time-series data, drag-and-drop dashboards, real-time alerts, and drill-down from site → asset. Monitors OEE, Availability, Uptime, plus AI-flagged anomalies. Integrates with OT systems.\n- **Sources:** [IBM Maximo Monitor (interlocsolutions)](https://www.interlocsolutions.com/blog/maximo-monitor-anomaly-detection-models) | [IBM Maximo Monitor datasheet](https://www.ibm.com/downloads/documents/us-en/10c31775a054017f) | [Banetti — Maximo Predict](https://info.banetti.com/ibm-maximo-predict/)\n\n---\n\n## Category 5: Leading Tool Dashboard {"parentUuid":"6eebec06-055c-4770-a53e-9fae5bd21140","isSidechain":true,"agentId":"a1fb0fb2cb5fa37d4","message":{"model":"claude-opus-4-8","id":"msg_01Fhxswr9B1N9fAn74P3W4d3","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"text","text":"All inputs are in. Here is the operational-intelligence roadmap.\n\n---\n\n# KNL Operational-Intelligence Roadmap\n\nRead-only audit of the FSM/rental/maintenance platform. No files were modified. Verdict, then a prioritized \"intelligence to add\" roadmap mapped to the data KNL already captures, then the few fields worth starting to capture.\n\n## Sources I read first-hand\n- KPI domain: `backend/crates/reporting/domain/src/lib.rs` (the 7 metrics + OpsSummary)\n- Price intelligence: `backend/crates/kernel/core/src/price_intel.rs`\n- Integrity domain: `backend/crates/compliance/integrity/src/domain.rs`\n- Reporting REST surface: `backend/crates/reporting/rest/src/lib.rs`\n- Schema: migrations `0007` (equipment), `0008` (work_orders + status_history), `0011` (p1_dispatch), `0014` (substitutions), `0015` (financial/cost ledger), `0018` (inspection schedules), `0022` (support), `0044` (acquisition cost/date)\n\nPlus three parallel agents (frontend audit, backend audit, data inventory) and one web-research agent (benchmarks + citations, all cited inline below).\n\n---\n\n## PART A — Verdict on current analytics\n\n### A1. What exists today\n\n**KpiPage / KpiDashboard** (`GET /api/v1/kpi`), 7 metrics, scoped Company/Region/Branch/Technician, per a single period:\n- `CompletedCount`, `weighted_completed_points` (P1=3/P2=2/P3=1)\n- `AverageResponseSpeed` = `first_in_progress_at − created_at`\n- `CompletionDurationAndDueCompliance` = `approved_at − created_at`, plus on-time-vs-`target_due_at`\n- `RevisitRate` (result_type=REVISIT_REQUIRED), `DelayRate` + reason distribution\n- `InspectionPlanCompletionRate`, `P1AcceptanceRate`\n\n**OpsDashboardPage** (`GET /api/v1/ops/summary`), all point-in-time counts: work-order funnel (received/assigned/in_progress/completed), aging WOs (>24h), P1 SLA breached / at-risk, top-10 mechanic load, equipment-status distribution (임대/예비/폐기/대체/매각), active substitutions, pending approvals, open support tickets.\n\n**ReportingPage** — Excel exports only (daily-status, work-diary). Not analytics; an operational artifact generator.\n\n**Integrity / anomaly engine** — exactly two detectors, both financial-governance: `anomaly.price_outlier` (the strong z-score/MAD/IQR/percentile stats in `price_intel.rs`, HIGH-side only = overpayment) and `anomaly.self_approval` (privileged user approves own purchase, fixed HIGH). Surfaced as triageable `governance_findings`.\n\n### A2. The honest assessment\n\n**What's genuinely valuable (keep):**\n- The Ops funnel + aging + P1 SLA breach/at-risk is real operational triage — a dispatcher acts on it today. Good.\n- `price_intel.rs` is the strongest piece of intelligence in the codebase: proper robust statistics, small-sample guard, confidence tiers, and it only flags overpayment (no false-positive theatre). It feeds a triage workflow with an action. This is the template the rest of the analytics should follow.\n- Revisit rate and delay-reason distribution are actionable quality signals.\n\n**The structural problems (fix):**\n\n1. **No trend, no baseline, no benchmark — anywhere.** Every KPI and every Ops number is a single value for a single period. You cannot see whether response time is improving or degrading, and nothing is compared to a target. A number with no direction and no target is close to a vanity metric. *Fix: add a previous-period delta and a configurable target line to every KPI tile; render a sparkline from period-over-period history.*\n\n2. **\"Completion time\" is mismeasured.** `CompletionDurationAndDueCompliance` uses `approved_at − created_at` — that's *administrative lead time* (intake → manager approval), not repair time. True technician work duration is reconstructable from `work_order_status_history` (every `to_status`/`occurred_at` transition is stored, migration 0008) but is not used. *Fix: compute true MTTR from status history (time in IN_PROGRESS) so the metric reflects field work, not paperwork.*\n\n3. **No drill-down.** The domain literally carries `work_order_ids` per rollup (`#[serde(skip_serializing)]`) and then drops them. So a manager sees \"revisit rate 14%\" and cannot click to the 14%. *Fix: expose the underlying WO list behind each metric.* This is the single highest-leverage UX fix — it converts every existing vanity number into an actionable one with near-zero new computation.\n\n4. **The analytics are work-order-centric, not asset-centric.** There is *zero equipment-reliability intelligence*: no MTBF, no per-asset failure count, no availability, no cost-per-asset, no repair-vs-replace — despite the data being present. For a forklift rental + maintenance business, the *asset* is the profit center, and it's the one thing the dashboards don't analyze.\n\n5. **The anomaly engine sees only money, never equipment.** Price-outlier + self-approval are procurement controls. There's no detector for an asset that's failing abnormally often, a PM that's overdue, or a technician whose revisit rate is an outlier — even though the same statistical engine (`compute_price_intel`) could score those distributions unchanged.\n\n---\n\n## PART B — Data KNL already captures (what's possible)\n\nConfirmed from migrations. The headline: **far more analytics are possible than are surfaced.**\n\n| Data asset | Table / migration | Unlocks |\n|---|---|---|\n| WO lifecycle transitions | `work_order_status_history (from/to_status, occurred_at)` · 0008 | True MTTR, time-in-stage, throughput trend |\n| WO → equipment link | `work_orders.equipment_id` · 0008 | Failures per asset → MTBF, Pareto/bad-actor |\n| WO result + delay | `result_type`, `delay_reason` · 0008 | First-time-fix, revisit, root-cause Pareto |\n| **Per-asset cost ledger** | `equipment_cost_ledger (equipment_id, work_order_id, amount_won, entry_at)` · 0015 | **Maintenance cost per asset, cost trend, MC/RAV** |\n| **Acquisition fact** | `registry_equipment.acquisition_cost_won, acquisition_date` · 0044 | **TCO, repair-vs-replace** |\n| Repair-vs-replace inputs | `financial_rental_quotes.cumulative_repair_cost_won, acquisition_value_won, current_residual_value_won` · 0015 | Repair/replace ratio already computed per quote |\n| Usage meter | `registry_equipment.hours BIGINT` (nullable) · 0007 | Usage-based PM, MTBF-per-hour *(point-in-time only — see Part D)* |\n| **PM schedules** | `regular_inspection_schedules (interval_days, due_date, status, completed_at)` · 0018 | **PM compliance, overdue PM, schedule compliance** |\n| Downtime proxy | `equipment_substitutions (source_equipment_id, assigned_at, returned_at)` · 0014 | Equipment downtime/availability (substitution = unit down) |\n| Rental status | `registry_equipment.status` 임대/예비/… + `rental_fee`, `rental_started_on` · 0007 | Rental utilization %, idle fleet |\n| Support SLA | `support_tickets (priority, due_at, resolved_at, closed_at)` · 0022 | SLA compliance %, resolution-time |\n| P1 response | `p1_dispatches (accept_window_started/ends_at)`, `responses.responded_at` · 0011 | Mean time to respond, SLA breach (partly used) |\n| Audit trail | `audit_events (action, actor, target, occurred_at)` · 0003 | Activity/throughput analytics on any entity |\n\n**Notable gaps in capture:** no time-series of `hours` (only the latest meter), no per-checklist-item pass/fail in `inspection_rounds`, no failure-code/cause taxonomy on work orders (delay_reason exists but not a structured root-cause code), no parts/inventory table (cost ledger captures spend amounts but not parts as line items).\n\n---\n\n## PART C — Prioritized \"intelligence to add\" roadmap\n\nOrdered high-value / low-effort first. Effort assumes the existing reporting crate + pure-domain pattern. Benchmarks are for the target lines to ship in the UI.\n\n### Tier 1 — High value, low effort (data fully present, mostly aggregation)\n\n**1. Drill-down on every existing KPI.** Stop dropping `work_order_ids`; return them and link each metric to its WO list. Effort: XS. Value: very high — fixes the \"data with no action\" problem across the whole KPI page at once.\n\n**2. Period-over-period trend + target line on every KPI/Ops tile.** Compare current vs prior period (delta %) and render a sparkline; add a config table of targets. Effort: S. Value: high. Targets to seed: response/repair improving, revisit < your baseline.\n\n**3. PM compliance & overdue PM.** From `regular_inspection_schedules`: `completed within ±10% of interval / scheduled`. Surface count + list of overdue assets. Benchmark line: **world-class ≥90%, below 80% = program not functioning** ([Fiix](https://fiixsoftware.com/maintenance-metrics/preventive-maintenance-compliance/), [MaintainX](https://www.getmaintainx.com/blog/preventive-maintenance-pm-compliance)). Effort: S. Value: very high — this is the #1 leading indicator in every CMMS and you already schedule PMs.\n\n**4. Maintenance cost per asset + cost trend.** `SUM(equipment_cost_ledger.amount_won) GROUP BY equipment_id`, over time. Rank assets by spend; trend month-over-month. Effort: S. Value: very high — direct money insight, and the input to #8/#9. Surfaced by every tool (UpKeep, Limble, Fiix \"report money spent by asset\").\n\n**5. True MTTR + first-time-fix rate.** MTTR from time-in-IN_PROGRESS in `work_order_status_history`; FTFR = `1 − revisit_rate` (you already compute revisit). Benchmarks: **MTTR world-class <6h vs 12–18h avg** ([oxmaint](https://oxmaint.com/article/mtbf-mttr-oee-maintenance-kpis)); **FTFR target 90%, industry avg 75–80%** ([2024 Field Service Benchmark Report](https://21176235.fs1.hubspotusercontent-na1.net/hubfs/21176235/ebook-2024-benchmarkreport-12-19.pdf), [IBM](https://www.ibm.com/think/topics/first-time-fix-rate)). Effort: S–M. Value: high.\n\n**6. Rental / fleet utilization.** From `registry_equipment.status`: `임대 / (임대+예비) × 100`; flag idle 예비 units carrying `rental_fee`. Benchmark: **65–75% healthy** ([Quipli](https://quipli.com/resources/top-kpis-for-a-rental-business/), [InTempo](https://www.intemposoftware.com/blog/equipment-rental-metrics-time-dollar-utilization)). Effort: S. Value: high — directly ties to rental revenue.\n\n### Tier 2 — High value, medium effort\n\n**7. MTBF + bad-actor (Pareto) per asset.** Failures per asset = corrective WOs per `equipment_id`; MTBF = operating time / failures. Pareto-rank: the **20% of assets driving 80% of WOs/cost** ([f7i.ai Pareto](https://f7i.ai/blog/pareto-analysis-in-maintenance-the-definitive-guide-to-the-8020-rule-for-industrial-reliability), [Reliabilityweb bad-actor](https://reliabilityweb.com/articles/entry/bad-actor-program)). Effort: M. Value: very high — this is *the* maintenance-intelligence flagship and the data exists.\n\n**8. Repair-vs-replace / TCO.** Per asset: `cumulative repair cost (cost ledger) vs acquisition_cost_won / residual`. Flag when cumulative repair exceeds a threshold of replacement value. Rule of thumb to encode: **repair > 50% of replacement value → replace** (also cited 65%/75% variants) ([Maintainly](https://maintainly.com/articles/understanding-the-75-maintenance-rule-in-asset-management-when-to-repair-or-replace), [Reliabilityweb LCA](https://reliabilityweb.com/articles/entry/repair-versus-replace-how-to-use-lifecycle-cost-analysis-to-determine-the-t)). Effort: M. Value: very high — turns the cost ledger into a capital-decision tool.\n\n**9. Equipment availability / downtime.** Downtime per asset from `equipment_substitutions (returned_at − assigned_at)` as proxy; `Availability = uptime/(uptime+downtime)`. Benchmark: **>92% world-class** ([oxmaint OEE](https://oxmaint.com/industries/manufacturing-plant/oee-calculation-formula-benchmark-manufacturing-improvement-strategies)). Effort: M. Value: high.\n\n**10. Support-ticket SLA compliance + resolution time.** `resolved_at` vs `due_at` → % within SLA; mean resolution by priority. Benchmark: **95%+ SLA compliance** ([ServiceTitan](https://www.servicetitan.com/blog/field-service-metrics)). Effort: S–M. Value: medium-high (data fully present, currently only a raw open-count).\n\n**11. Planned-vs-unplanned ratio.** Inspection/PM WOs vs corrective WOs. Benchmark: **80–90% planned world-class, 50–65% avg** ([Limble](https://limble.com/blog/planned-vs-unplanned-maintenance-ratio), [MaintainX PMP](https://www.getmaintainx.com/learning-center/planned-maintenance-percentage)). Effort: S. Value: medium-high — single best maturity indicator.\n\n### Tier 3 — High value, higher effort / needs new capture\n\n**12. Reliability/quality anomaly detectors** reusing `compute_price_intel` unchanged on new distributions: per-asset failure frequency, per-technician revisit rate, overdue-PM. Same triage workflow as price-outlier. Effort: M (engine exists). Value: high.\n\n**13. Maintenance cost as % of RAV** (portfolio-level). Needs replacement-asset-value per asset; `vehicle_value`/`acquisition_cost_won` is a serviceable proxy. Benchmark: **2–3% world-class** ([Fiix MC/RAV](https://fiixsoftware.com/maintenance-metrics/mcrav/), SMRP). Effort: M.\n\n**14. Technician utilization / wrench time.** Needs reliable per-WO active-work duration (Tier-1 #5 gets you time-in-stage; true wrench time needs clock-in/out). Benchmarks: **utilization 75–80% world-class; wrench time 25–35% typical** ([FieldEdge](https://fieldedge.com/blog/technician-utilization-benchmarks/), [Certify Hub](https://thecertifyhub.com/wrenchtime/)). Effort: M–L.\n\n**15. Predictive / usage-based PM.** Trigger PM by accumulated operating hours (forklift standard **every 250–500 hours**) — requires the hours time-series in Part D. Effort: L.\n\n---\n\n## PART D — Data to START capturing (unlocks the high-value tier)\n\n1. **Equipment hours time-series** (a `equipment_hour_readings` table: equipment_id, hours, read_at). Today `registry_equipment.hours` is a single overwrite-in-place value. A history unlocks **usage-based PM, MTBF-per-operating-hour, and predictive signals** (hours/usage triggers) — the highest-value predictive capability and currently impossible. *Biggest single unlock.*\n\n2. **Structured failure/root-cause code on work orders** (a small controlled vocabulary, beyond free-text `delay_reason`). Pareto/RCA quality degrades badly when cause is \"Unknown\" in >40% of WOs ([f7i.ai](https://f7i.ai/blog/pareto-analysis-in-maintenance-the-definitive-guide-to-the-8020-rule-for-industrial-reliability)). Enables real bad-actor *root-cause* analysis, not just frequency.\n\n3. **Explicit downtime stamps on work orders** (down_at / restored_at), so availability doesn't have to lean on the substitution proxy (a substitution isn't created for every failure).\n\n4. **Per-item inspection results** in `inspection_rounds` (currently pass/fail per checklist item isn't stored). Enables failed-inspection-item trending and condition-based signals.\n\n5. **Parts as line items** in the cost ledger (currently a lump `amount_won` + memo). Unlocks **MRO inventory turns and parts-spend analysis** ([f7i.ai MRO](https://f7i.ai/blog/inventory-turns-in-mro-the-definitive-guide-to-optimizing-spare-parts-in-2026)) — otherwise not possible.\n\n6. **CSAT capture** on work-order/support close (1–5). Field-service benchmark **CSAT 85–90%, NPS 50–70** ([ServiceTitan](https://www.servicetitan.com/blog/field-service-metrics), [Retently 2025](https://www.retently.com/blog/good-net-promoter-score/)).\n\n---\n\n## Bottom line\nThe current analytics are **operationally real but shallow and money-only**: a good Ops triage board and a genuinely strong price-anomaly engine, sitting next to a KPI page of point-in-time numbers with no trend, no target, no drill-down, and a completion metric that measures paperwork instead of repair. The asset — the actual profit center of a forklift rental/maintenance business — is the one thing the intelligence layer ignores, even though the cost ledger (0015), acquisition facts (0044), PM schedules (0018), and WO-to-equipment links (0008) make MTBF, PM compliance, cost-per-asset, TCO/repair-vs-replace, and bad-actor Pareto all buildable on existing data. Highest ROI: (1) wire drill-down + trend/target onto the KPIs you already compute, then (2) ship the asset-centric tier (PM compliance, cost-per-asset, MTBF/bad-actor, repair-vs-replace), then (3) start the equipment-hours time-series to open the predictive door."}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"stop_details":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":2858,"cache_creation_input_tokens":386,"cache_read_input_tokens":88564,"output_tokens":6560,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":386},"inference_geo":"not_available","iterations":[{"input_tokens":2858,"output_tokens":6560,"cache_read_input_tokens":88564,"cache_creation_input_tokens":386,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":386,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"type":"message"}],"speed":"standard"},"diagnostics":null},"requestId":"req_011CcLc4gWESkNZtZkMVnnF3","attributionAgent":"general-purpose","type":"assistant","uuid":"6c11cd79-7d96-4e92-9100-92be0d8f0620","timestamp":"2026-06-23T17:44:33.757Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/jasonlee/Developer/maintenance","sessionId":"a4f6c1da-da69-4ccc-b409-be462b15706d","version":"2.1.185","gitBranch":"feat/multi-tenant-phase1","slug":"flickering-finding-valiant"}
